    function loadScript(url, callback) {
      var script = document.createElement("script");
      script.type = "text/javascript";
    
      if (script.readyState) {  //Internet Explorer
          script.onreadystatechange = function() {
            if (script.readyState == "loaded" ||
                    script.readyState == "complete") {
              script.onreadystatechange = null;
              callback();
            }
          };
      } else {  //Other browsers
        script.onload = function() {
          callback();
        };
      }
    
      script.src = url;
      document.getElementsByTagName("head")[0].appendChild(script);
    }

      AppleID.auth.init({

<div id="review_426610054" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/426610054" />
    <a title="Stephanie Jay" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/12913244-stephanie-jay"><img alt="Stephanie Jay" src="https://s.gr-assets.com/assets/nophoto/user/u_50x66-632230dc9882b4352d753eedf9396530.png" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/426610054?book_show_action=true">Oct 02, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Stephanie Jay" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Stephanie Jay" href="/user/show/12913244-stephanie-jay">Stephanie Jay</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer426610054" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer88075002806858214"> This book was a pretty good! It was a little overdramatic in some parts though. I think the title fits the book well! It says "Tales from a Not-So-Popular Party Girl," and it is about a girl named Nikki, who is unpopular, setting up a Halloween party for her school. She must make a dance for the students in her school. I think this book title suits the book well also, because "Dork Diaries" is a good name for a unpopular girl writing a diary.<br/> If I had to be one of the characters in this book it</span>
  <span id="freeText88075002806858214" style="display:none"> This book was a pretty good! It was a little overdramatic in some parts though. I think the title fits the book well! It says "Tales from a Not-So-Popular Party Girl," and it is about a girl named Nikki, who is unpopular, setting up a Halloween party for her school. She must make a dance for the students in her school. I think this book title suits the book well also, because "Dork Diaries" is a good name for a unpopular girl writing a diary.<br /> If I had to be one of the characters in this book it would be Brianna, Nikki's little sister. Her sister and her make squirt guns to kill the tooth fairy, because Brianna is afraid of the tooth fairy. It sounds like Brianna is a funny little squirt too! She annoys her sister sometimes, but it's funny. She is a fun character in this book.<br /> This book made me laugh, laugh in pity of some of the characters, and frown. I laughed at some parts of this book, like when Brianna wanted to kill the tooth fairy. I laughed in pity at some parts when she said "Mackenzie", the mean girl,"is such a jerk! I HATE HER!" That was a little too overdramatic! I also frowned when some parts of this book didn't make sense. Overall this was a pretty good book!</span>
  <a data-text-id="88075002806858214" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<span id="freeTextContainer4813962641722087654">Dork Diaries is an amazing series. I like this book because, your life might be like Nikki's when you're a teenager. For example, Nikki tries to be at 2 parties at the same time. That might be something you might do. Sometimes it's okay to just please one person instead of everybody at the same time. Another reason I like this book is because it's really funny. There's more funny parts in one chapter than in any of the other books I've read. The last reason I like this book is because it teaches life lessons. I love this book and you will too.</span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer415397093" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer950852157119281012">The second of the Dork Diaries books, Rachel Renee Russell hit a whole in one again with her equally, funny, purple-covered female version of Diary of a Wimpy Kid. Nikki's tween voice rings true yet again with her worries about being popular, the craziness of her family and friends, and the troubles she has with mean girl Mackenzie (I just HATE when she sashays!) and her oh-so-adorable crush Brandon. 4/5 because, like Dork Diaries #1, this book is truthful, happy and easy to understand, while al</span>
  <span id="freeText950852157119281012" style="display:none">The second of the Dork Diaries books, Rachel Renee Russell hit a whole in one again with her equally, funny, purple-covered female version of Diary of a Wimpy Kid. Nikki's tween voice rings true yet again with her worries about being popular, the craziness of her family and friends, and the troubles she has with mean girl Mackenzie (I just HATE when she sashays!) and her oh-so-adorable crush Brandon. 4/5 because, like Dork Diaries #1, this book is truthful, happy and easy to understand, while also being funny and a correct portrayal of a 13ish year old's life. Now all they have to do is make a movie of the series, right? That's what they did with Diary of a Wimpy Kid! Why not, hey?</span>

    <a title="izzy" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/9283091-izzy"><img alt="izzy" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1529046654p2/9283091.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/853451443?book_show_action=true">Feb 12, 2014</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="izzy" class="user" itemprop="url" name="izzy" href="/user/show/9283091-izzy">izzy</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Hardcover 9781416980087" href="/book/show/7208637-tales-from-a-not-so-popular-party-girl">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/9283091-izzy?shelf=middle-grade">middle-grade</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/9283091-izzy?shelf=re-reading">re-reading</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/9283091-izzy?shelf=contemporary">contemporary</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/9283091-izzy?shelf=series">series</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/9283091-izzy?shelf=own-a-copy">own-a-copy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/9283091-izzy?shelf=3-stars">3-stars</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer853451443" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer12016874969136127244"><b>My Rating: 3/5 stars</b><br/><br/>(Before we begin this review, I would just like to clarify that I will not be reading the whole series; I will only be rereading the books I own just to get back onto track with my reading goal for this year.)<br/><br/>Okay, I'll admit. I liked this slightly better than the first one. Nikki was a little less annoying (although she's not quite tolerable just yet) than the first book, and I definitely had a better understanding of her character. I also really liked the plot a lot more. I</span>
  <span id="freeText12016874969136127244" style="display:none"><b>My Rating: 3/5 stars</b><br /><br />(Before we begin this review, I would just like to clarify that I will not be reading the whole series; I will only be rereading the books I own just to get back onto track with my reading goal for this year.)<br /><br />Okay, I'll admit. I liked this slightly better than the first one. Nikki was a little less annoying (although she's not quite tolerable just yet) than the first book, and I definitely had a better understanding of her character. I also really liked the plot a lot more. It was also really cute, and definitely a lot more... Solid. In the first book the plot was flying all over the place, as opposed to this book where all the events in Nikki's diary entry built up to the dance.<br /><br />I still don't like the over-exaggerations in some parts, though. Nikki literally is so ungrateful in some parts and Mackenzie is too mean to be real. I really wish that Russell would stop painting her characters as such bitches so that her target audience would not get the wrong idea, that the only popular girls are the mean ones and that you should always whine and complain if things don't go your way.<br /><br />Overall, this book was slightly better; although, I still didn't like it <i>that</i> much. I hope that the next book will become even better.<br /><br /><b>What's next on my reading list?</b> THE TRUTH ABOUT FOREVER by Sarah Dessen.</span>
  <a data-text-id="12016874969136127244" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<span id="freeTextContainer9586033166790503168">Nikki Maxwell's troubles are far from over! Mackenzie has invited her to her birthday party again! But this time she actually goes just so she can talk to Brandon and hopefully get him to invite her to the Halloween party! But before she can even talk to him Mackenzie bullies her into leaving the party :( The next big party coming up is the Halloween party, and Nikki, Zoey, and Chloe have agreed to be on the planning committee – which really only means that if the party fails they'll be the one'</span>
  <span id="freeText9586033166790503168" style="display:none">Nikki Maxwell's troubles are far from over! Mackenzie has invited her to her birthday party again! But this time she actually goes just so she can talk to Brandon and hopefully get him to invite her to the Halloween party! But before she can even talk to him Mackenzie bullies her into leaving the party :( The next big party coming up is the Halloween party, and Nikki, Zoey, and Chloe have agreed to be on the planning committee – which really only means that if the party fails they'll be the one's the whole school blames! One Halloween party quickly turns into three – how is Nikki supposed to be in three places at once? <br /><br />I know I said the first book was pretty terrible, but I already had the second one checked out from the library, as well as a beautiful sunny day so I decided to go ahead and read it on the back deck. I didn't find it to be as annoying to read as the first, but the writing was still very ditzy! <br /><br />I loved how this book was written in 2010 and is supposed to be from the perspective of a 14 year old girl obsessed with fashion and getting the latest iPhone, and yet she also dreamed of having a DVD/VCR in her locker! I don't know anyone under 20 who even knows what a VHS is.</span>

<span id="freeTextContainer11812854585323905507">	Summary…. Dork Diaries: Tales from a not-so Popular Party Girl is about a girl named Nikki. It is basically a girl’s diary. It talks about her crush, her enemy, her sister, and about what’s going on in her life. Her life I very crazy and interesting. <br/>	She has to deal with being three different things in one night. She has to be at a birthday party, a Halloween party dressed as trash bags with her friends, and the same Halloween party, but dressed as a princess with her date Brandon. Brandon is </span>
  <span id="freeText11812854585323905507" style="display:none">	Summary…. Dork Diaries: Tales from a not-so Popular Party Girl is about a girl named Nikki. It is basically a girl’s diary. It talks about her crush, her enemy, her sister, and about what’s going on in her life. Her life I very crazy and interesting. <br />	She has to deal with being three different things in one night. She has to be at a birthday party, a Halloween party dressed as trash bags with her friends, and the same Halloween party, but dressed as a princess with her date Brandon. Brandon is her crush and he asked her to the dance. She has to run back and forth getting changed.<br />	Main Characters…. Nikki and Mackenzie are the main characters. Mackenzie is Nikki’s enemy. Mackenzie is always trying to get Nikki, she made her wear a dirty rat costume. Nikki does not like Mackenzie because she is always mean to her.<br />	Setting…. The setting of this book is in a lot of places. One place is Nikki’s school. A few other places are Nikki’s house and the zoo. The zoo is wear she had to go to the dance at dressed in a rat costume.<br />	Conflict…. One conflict is that she needs to be two places at once. Dressed in three different costumes. She has to go back and forth. She was supposed hang out with her friends and her date at the dance [which is one of the places she needed to be].<br />	Resolution…. She fixes her problem by running where she needs to go. She has to run from building to building. Nikki gets dressed in the bathrooms. She has to make up excuses, like “I have to use the bathroom. I will be back.” Or “I’m going to go get more food”.<br />	Opinion…. My opinion on this book is that it is an entertaining book. It is an easy read. If you want a quick book read this book. If you have read the other Dork Diaries books you should read this one. <br />	Recommendation…. I recommend this book because it is fun to read. If you like funny books you should read this one. I know that you will like this book. In Dork Dairies you get to read someone else’s life and go through it with them.<br /></span>

<span id="freeTextContainer6896906135415539206">Rating: 5<br/><br/>This book picks up where the first one left off, which I think is great because I feel that we get to know Nikki Maxell better with each book and they don't feel rushed. Nikki and her new friends come together to make the Halloween party happen, but Nikki also double books herself helping out another party. What's a girl to do with tw</span>
  <span id="freeText6896906135415539206" style="display:none">Rating: 5<br /><br />This book picks up where the first one left off, which I think is great because I feel that we get to know Nikki Maxell better with each book and they don't feel rushed. I feel that I could be reading a 14 year old's diary. So this book is about overcoming a BIG obstacle after Mackenzie decides to ruin the Halloween Dance. Nikki and her new friends come together to make the Halloween party happen, but Nikki also double books herself helping out another party. What's a girl to do with two parties to attend, a mean girl that will stop at nothing to make her life hell, a cute crush that asks her to the dance and two krazy friends that she is still getting to know? Well you'll have to find out like I did by reading the book.<br /><br />I HIGHLY RECOMMEND TO YOUNG READERS AND ALL YOUNG AT HEART READERS ALIKE! </span>

<div id="review_1359772145" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1359772145" />
    <a title="Lanie" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/22024407-lanie"><img alt="Lanie" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1396208561p2/22024407.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1359772145?book_show_action=true">Aug 10, 2015</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Lanie" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Lanie" href="/user/show/22024407-lanie">Lanie</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/22024407-lanie?shelf=realistic-fiction">realistic-fiction</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/22024407-lanie?shelf=crappy-main-characters">crappy-main-characters</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/22024407-lanie?shelf=middle-grade">middle-grade</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/22024407-lanie?shelf=shouldn-t-like-but-do-anyway">shouldn-t-like-but-do-anyway</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1359772145" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer2125241056209517793">"Tales from a not so popular party girl " is the 2nd book in the dork diaries series, a sort of girls version of diary of a wimpy kid. This book was definitely an improvement over the 1st. Yes, it's still very shallow, focusing on rather trivial things, it was still kinda fun in a mindless preteen fad sort of way. Popular "mean" girls, pretty dresses, and school dances might not be very important in the long run, but to a teenage girl, these things are the center of their universe. The main char</span>
  <span id="freeText2125241056209517793" style="display:none">"Tales from a not so popular party girl " is the 2nd book in the dork diaries series, a sort of girls version of diary of a wimpy kid. This book was definitely an improvement over the 1st. Yes, it's still very shallow, focusing on rather trivial things, it was still kinda fun in a mindless preteen fad sort of way. Popular "mean" girls, pretty dresses, and school dances might not be very important in the long run, but to a teenage girl, these things are the center of their universe. The main character, Nikki, is still obnoxious &amp; self centered/serving, but seemed a bit more bearable here. The plot was more focused too, instead of what felt like random events strung loosely together, it all lead up to the big finish at the Halloween bash. While still feeling like individual diary entries. It's actually pretty funny and the art work ads to the story. The whole one upping the mean girl is a tried and true plot line, and while well worn, I can really see why a young girl would find such a series so entertaining. :)<br /><br />Actually, Nikki, wasn't even my big issue of today's read. It was her friends, Choey &amp; Zoey. They are just to forgiving to be really. Real teenage girls aren't going to be so quick to forgive such dumb choices. Plus, they make my cat look smart. What sort of idiots really think that bags of thrash would be a good costume?! After all that crap in book 1 were they want to impress the "c c &amp; p" girls with the tattoo thing, you'd think they'd stick with the pretty outfits.... But nope! They dress as bags of trash? Why? To make their "bff" Nikki happy. Cute in a dumb kinda way..... But mostly I think the choice was for the sake of plot convince. For the sole purpose of making the night more difficult for our m.c.<br /><br /><br />But really, it was pretty fun. :) I enjoyed it, &amp; will likely read it again.</span>
  <a data-text-id="2125241056209517793" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_1755930671" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1755930671" />
    <a title="Marlee B" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/59563806-marlee-b"><img alt="Marlee B" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1473780261p2/59563806.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1755930671?book_show_action=true">Sep 19, 2016</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Marlee B" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Marlee B" href="/user/show/59563806-marlee-b">Marlee B</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/59563806-marlee-b?shelf=first-nine-weeks">first-nine-weeks</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1755930671" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer15441343704844409831">Nikki Maxwell is a Westchester Country middle school student at the age of 14 she has a lot of drama in her life because of the CCP girls (cute,cool and popular) and her crush Brandon. In this book Nikki is locker Neighbors right next to the most popular of the CCP girls Mackenzie Hollister. Both girls are trying to win over there crush Brandon there is one problem Nikki is a dork. This is a recipe for disaster: 4 party's,2 friends,1 crush. Divided by 1 mean girl. Chloe and Zoe Nikki's best frie</span>
  <span id="freeText15441343704844409831" style="display:none">Nikki Maxwell is a Westchester Country middle school student at the age of 14 she has a lot of drama in her life because of the CCP girls (cute,cool and popular) and her crush Brandon. In this book Nikki is locker Neighbors right next to the most popular of the CCP girls Mackenzie Hollister. Both girls are trying to win over there crush Brandon there is one problem Nikki is a dork. This is a recipe for disaster: 4 party's,2 friends,1 crush. Divided by 1 mean girl. Chloe and Zoe Nikki's best friends try to step in and help out but everything and everyone end up in huge mess. Nikki is juggling too much she's trying to plan her little sisters ballet party and go to the Halloween dance. Can she juggle 2 events at once at the exact same time. I like this book because I can feel how stressed out Nikki was in this situation. I get cringy every time. I often found myself excited just for the next chapter.I could never stop. I think that this book is mainly for girls that like lots of drama. I feel this book is just like Diary of a Wimpy kid except Dork Diaries is just for girls. I can't wait for y'all to read it!!</span>
  <a data-text-id="15441343704844409831" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  <span id="freeText8754429762354677425" style="display:none">I decided to dive in and try one of these since they are so popular. I was disappointed. The characters are all so boring and formulaic with "mean girls" who are over-the-top and such contrived drama on every page. Then there is the random weird stuff (like going to a funeral of someone her parents don't even know and hiccuping through the whole thing) where our main character embarrasses herself, again. I don't even like the illustrations that make the girls look all doe-eyed, big-haired, skinny, and in general all glamoured out. <br /><br />If you are looking for a great "girl" diary skip these and read something with substance like the <i>Popularity Papers<i>. </i></i></span>

  function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked && exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&name=' + shelf_name + '&a=' + action + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('4wtEqlMDAf2MlwU8N/QT/pFBlw//f80jLAE/oIFQ70p1M5ReCU2pjxX35bAW+LpNVTYMTOu8VqB599Urq7395g==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

  function refreshGroupBox(group_id, book_id) {

  }
